     Impact Dashboard — Bootstrap + First Slice

     Context

     We are building an engineering impact dashboard for a GitHub repo (PostHog
     as the primary target, but the tool must be repo-agnostic). The audience is
      busy engineering leaders who want meaningful signal beyond LOC / commit /
     PR counts.

     A detailed 15-question grilling session resolved the design (see arch.md at
      repo root). The agreed shape:

     - Three pillars (Delivery / Collaboration / Quality), each composed of
     structurally honest sub-metrics that survive Goodhart's law.
     - Risk = blast radius (criticality × files × cross-module breadth × test
     ratio), not LOC.
     - Bus factor + work mix as descriptive panels, not scored.
     - AI summary grounded in cited evidence, weekly cached.
     - Standouts (multi-axis) instead of a single Top Contributor leaderboard.
     - Soft-degrade on every optional input (test files, CI data, labels).

     The current repo is a Svelte 5 + Hono + Drizzle + SQLite starter with a
     Todo example. The Todo example is scaffolding to be removed before
     dashboard work begins.

     Bootstrap (already executed before plan mode kicked in)

     - arch.md written at repo root with all decisions from the grilling
     session.
     - lib/core/Api.ts created with get / post wrappers (named functions, object
      export, throw on non-2xx) — matches the user's stated convention (export 
     const Api = { get, post }).
     - Removed: client/todo/ (folder), server/Todos.ts, todos table in
     db/schema.ts, todo type in client/types.ts.
     - Updated: server/index.ts (dropped Todos init), client/app/App.svelte
     (dropped Todo route), client/app/Header.svelte (dropped Todos link).
     - db/schema.ts and client/types.ts left as empty placeholders so dashboard
     schema/types can land cleanly.
     - grep confirmed no lingering Todo references in .ts / .svelte files.

     BE Slice 1 — DONE

     Schema + GitHub PR ingest landed:
     - server/Config.ts (env + JSON config, throws on missing GITHUB_TOKEN)
     - server/Github.ts (REST client, recursive rate-limit retry)
     - server/Sync.ts (recursive paginated ingest, cursor in sync_state)
     - server/Pulls.ts (POST /api/sync, GET /api/pulls)
     - db/schema.ts (authors, pulls, sync_state)
     - config.example.json, .env.empty, .gitignore updated, dotenv/config wired
     in server/index.ts

     Sync + pulls confirmed working end-to-end against a real repo.

     Original BE Slice 1 spec (for reference)

     Locked answers:
     - Auth: GITHUB_TOKEN env var, fine-grained PAT, read-only on target repo.
     - Target repo: config-driven from day 1 (no hardcode).
     - Fetch: REST API for v1 (GraphQL deferred).

     Files to create

     server/
       Config.ts        — reads GITHUB_TOKEN from env, target repo from config
     file,
                          bot exclusion list. Pattern: function load(): Config;
     export const Config = { load }.

       Github.ts        — REST client for the GitHub PRs endpoint.
                          Pulls
     /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls?state=all&sort=updated&direction=asc
                          paginated, with token auth. Functions:
     fetchPullsSince(cursor),
                          returns batches of raw PR objects + next cursor.
                          Handles 401/403/404 with clear errors.
                          Handles 403/429 rate-limit (Retry-After /
     X-RateLimit-Reset) by waiting.

       Sync.ts          — orchestrates incremental ingest. Reads cursor from
     syncState,
                          loops fetchPullsSince batches, normalizes + upserts
     into db,
                          writes new cursor. Exposes function syncPulls():
     Promise<{ added: number }>.

       Pulls.ts         — Hono routes:
                            POST /api/sync   — triggers Sync.syncPulls, returns
     count
                            GET  /api/pulls  — debug: returns last N rows
     (limit, offset)
                          Pattern: function init(app, db) + export const Pulls =
      { init }.

     Files to update

     db/schema.ts       — define tables:
                            authors    (login PK, name, isBot flag derived at
     insert)
                            pulls      (id PK = GitHub PR node_id, number, repo,
      title,
                                        state, author_login FK→authors, body,
     createdAt,
                                        updatedAt, closedAt, mergedAt,
     draftCreatedAt nullable,
                                        isDraft, mergedBy, baseRef, headRef,
     labels JSON,
                                        additions, deletions, changedFiles)
                            syncState  (key PK, value text, updatedAt) — stores
     cursor like
                                        { key: 'pulls:posthog/posthog', value:
     '<iso-timestamp>' }

     config.json        — at repo root, gitignored sample committed as
     config.example.json:
                            {
                              "repo": "posthog/posthog",
                              "bots": ["dependabot*", "renovate*",
     "github-actions*", "*[bot]"]
                            }
                          Config.load reads this; later slices add criticality /
      weights.

     .env.example       — GITHUB_TOKEN=ghp_xxx

     server/index.ts    — import Db, Pulls; call Pulls.init(app, Db.get()).

     .gitignore         — add config.json, .env (verify existing entries first).

     Drizzle / DB setup

     - db/schema.ts uses existing sqliteTable pattern (matches removed todos
     table style).
     - Run npm run db:push to materialize the schema in data/sqlite.db.
     - server/Db.ts already wired correctly — no changes needed.

     Github fetch contract

     - Endpoint: GET https://api.github.com/repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls?state=all
     &sort=updated&direction=asc&per_page=100&page=N
     - Headers: Authorization: Bearer ${GITHUB_TOKEN}, Accept: 
     application/vnd.github+json, X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28.
     - Pagination: walk page= until response is empty.
     - Cursor: stored as the max updated_at seen. Next sync resumes by filtering
      client-side (REST endpoint sorts ascending by updated; we stop persisting
     once we've processed everything > cursor).
     - Note: the list endpoint does NOT return additions, deletions,
     changed_files, or merge metadata. Those need a per-PR detail fetch (GET 
     /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{number}). For this slice we store what the
     list endpoint gives us and leave detail-fetch fields nullable — detail
     enrichment is a separate slice (it costs 1 request per PR, so it's
     expensive and needs its own backfill strategy).

     Conventions to follow (from existing repo)

     - Feature modules: named-function declarations, single object export (e.g.
     export const Sync = { syncPulls }).
     - No arrow-const for functions. Explicit types on args / returns. No any.
     - Use path aliases $server, $db, $lib.
     - Soft-degrade: if GITHUB_TOKEN missing, Config.load throws with a clear
     actionable error — do not silently fall back to unauth (60/hr is useless).

     FE Slice 1 — Dashboard shell consuming real PR data

     Now that sync + pulls work, build the FE shell in the dashboard's actual
     shape (per-engineer cards, sync trigger). Show only the signals we can
     honestly compute today from raw PR rows; pillar bars stay as visible
     placeholders ("pending") until later slices land reviews / files / metrics.
      No fake numbers.

     Data we can honestly surface today

     - Engineer list = distinct non-bot authors from pulls (joined with
     authors.isBot = false).
     - Per engineer: PR-authored count, last activity (max updated_at), first
     activity (min created_at), merged count, draft count.
     - Repo-level: total PRs, total non-bot authors, last sync timestamp (from
     sync_state).
     - All filtering by analysis window happens server-side; v1 hardcodes
     rolling-90d (window controls are a follow-up slice — keep this slice
     tight).

     Files to create

     server/
       Engineers.ts    — Hono routes:
                           GET /api/engineers      → { engineers: [...],
     summary: {...} }
                           GET /api/sync/status    → { lastSync: iso|null,
     cursorAt: iso|null, totalPulls }
                         Pure aggregation on `pulls` joined with `authors` where
      isBot=false,
                         filtered to updatedAt >= now - 90d (server-computed
     cutoff).
                         Pattern: function init(app, db) + export const
     Engineers = { init }.

     client/dashboard/
       Dashboard.ts            — Api wrapper. Functions: loadEngineers(),
     runSync(), loadStatus().
                                 export const Dashboard = { loadEngineers,
     runSync, loadStatus }.
       Dashboard.svelte        — page: SyncBar + grid of EngineerCards.
                                 Loads engineers on mount; refreshes after sync.
       SyncBar.svelte          — sync button, last-sync timestamp, total-PRs
     counter.
                                 Disabled state while syncing, shows added count
      after.
       EngineerCard.svelte     — login + small avatar fallback (initials),
                                 PR count + merged count + first/last activity
     dates,
                                 three greyed-out placeholder pillar bars
     labeled
                                 "Delivery / Collaboration / Quality — pending".

     Files to update

     server/index.ts          — import Engineers; call Engineers.init(app, db).
     client/app/App.svelte    — add `dashboard` route; make it the default
     landing
                                (replaces Home as default; Home stays reachable
     via nav).
     client/app/Header.svelte — add Dashboard nav link, keep Home + About.
     lib/Router.ts            — change default route from 'home' to 'dashboard'.

     Type contracts

     // shared between server response and client consumer
     type engineer = {
       login: string
       prCount: number
       mergedCount: number
       draftCount: number
       firstActivity: string  // iso
       lastActivity: string   // iso
     }

     type summary = {
       totalPulls: number
       totalEngineers: number
       windowDays: number
     }

     type syncStatus = {
       lastSync: string | null
       cursorAt: string | null
       totalPulls: number
     }

     Conventions

     - Components: Svelte 5 runes ($state, $derived), onMount for initial load.
     - All HTTP calls go through lib/core/Api.ts (Api.get, Api.post). No raw
     fetch in client modules.
     - Functional style (no arrow-const for top-level functions, no let, no for
     — same lint rules as BE).
     - Honest placeholders: the three pillar bars render but are visibly
     disabled/greyed with a "pending" label. Do not show fake values.

     Out of scope for this slice

     - Pillar metrics (Delivery / Collaboration / Quality computation).
     - Window controls (rolling/calendar toggle, 30/90/365 sizing).
     - Standouts panel, concentration risks, AI summary, work mix.
     - Reviews / files / check runs ingest.
     - Engineer drilldown / profile page.
     - Styling polish — utilitarian CSS is fine for v1.

     Verification

     - npm run check — TS + svelte-check clean.
     - npm run lint — prettier + eslint clean.
     - npm run dev — server boots; visiting / lands on the dashboard.
     - Dashboard renders: sync bar at top, engineer grid below.
     - Click sync button → POSTs /api/sync → engineer grid refreshes with real
     authors after sync completes (or immediately if data already in DB).
     - Each card shows login + real PR count + three greyed-out "pending" pillar
      bars.
     - Navigating between Dashboard / Home / About via Header works (route store
      updates, no page reload).

     Critical files referenced

     - arch.md — design tree.

     - lib/Router.ts — route store + navigate (existing; default route updated).
     - db/schema.ts — authors, pulls, sync_state (existing; no changes).
     - server/Db.ts — Drizzle handle (no changes).
     - server/index.ts — register Engineers.init alongside Pulls.init.
     - client/app/App.svelte, client/app/Header.svelte — route + nav stitch.

● Time-boxed reality check. You've spent significant time on grilling +
  bootstrap. The assessment is 1.5hr total; remaining budget is probably 60–75
  min. Let me re-prioritize ruthlessly against the rubric.

  What the rubric actually rewards

  - Top 5 with clear "why" — currently we sort by mergedCount and call it
  impact. Not enough.
  - Real metrics, not placeholders — the three greyed-out pillar bars are a
  problem on submission.
  - No mystery numbers — every metric must be explained inline (tooltip /
  methodology section).
  - Single page on laptop — currently scrollable, fine but tighten.
  - Hosted — not done.
  - AI narrative — value-add, not required.

  What we can compute today (PR data only)

  Already in DB: created_at, merged_at, closed_at, is_draft, labels, title,
  body. That gets us:

  - Delivery: median cycle time, merged count, active weeks (distinct YYYY-WW in
   mergedAt), follow-through (merged/opened ratio).
  - Quality (partial): revert-touched count (detect ^Revert  titles → which PRs
  were reverted, attribute to original author).
  - Work mix: keyword/label classification (feat/fix/chore from title or
  labels).

  Missing without more data: review depth, review breadth, files touched, bus
  factor.

  Hard call: do we ingest reviews? Adding /api/repos/.../pulls/{n}/reviews per
  PR for 90 days = ~500–1500 requests against PostHog. At GitHub's rate ~50/s
  authenticated, that's 30–60s. ~20 min of dev to wire it. Big payoff —
  Collaboration pillar becomes real (reviews given, breadth = distinct authors
  reviewed). Without reviews, Collaboration stays empty.

  Recommended slice (~75 min budget)

  Step: 1
  Time: 20 min
  What: Reviews ingest — reviews table + GraphQL or REST batch fetch for PRs in
    90d window
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 2
  Time: 15 min
  What: Compute real impact — per-engineer aggregations (cycle, merged, active
    weeks, follow-through, reviews given, breadth, revert-touched). Composite  =

    weighted normalized score. Replace placeholder bars.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 3
  Time: 15 min
  What: Top 5 panel + methodology — top of page: 5 cards with score + 2–3 reason

    bullets per engineer. Tooltip/expander explaining each metric and weight.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 4
  Time: 10 min
  What: Gemini narrative — POST /api/ai/enrich/:login for top-5 only, real
    metrics + top PR titles in prompt, cached. Gemini 1.5/2.0 Flash for cost.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 5
  Time: 10 min
  What: One-page fit + deploy — tighten viewport, deploy to Render (Docker) or
    Fly.io with SQLite volume

  Cuts vs arch.md: drop bus factor, drop work-mix bar, drop pagination (top 5 +
  brief table below), drop window-control toggle, drop standouts panel.
  Composite IS shown (rubric wants top-5 ranking — leaderboard concern is
  academic for this exercise).

  Defensible impact definition (write into the methodology panel):

  ▎ Impact = consistent shipping (active weeks × merged count, 
  ▎ cycle-time–adjusted) + collaboration (reviews given, breadth of authors 
  ▎ reviewed) + quality (follow-through, low revert-touch rate). Computed over 
  ▎ the last 90 days, excluding bots and accounts with fewer than 3 merged PRs.

  Two questions to lock the plan

  1. Reviews ingest yes/no? Recommended yes — without it Collaboration is fake
  and the rubric punishes that. ~20 min cost.
  2. Deployment target? Recommend Render with a Dockerfile (free tier,
  persistent disk, simplest from a fresh repo). Alternatives: Fly.io (better for
   SQLite, free tier shrunk), or ngrok tunnel as a fallback if deployment
  chokes.

  Confirm those two and I'll start with reviews ingest immediately — every
  minute on planning past this is sunk cost.

❯ I will be hosting on vercel                                                   

● Vercel is a problem for our current arch (SQLite + long-running sync). But
  there's a clean pivot that's actually better for this assessment.

  Recommendation: pre-build static, deploy to Vercel

  Pivot: keep the Hono backend for local dev, but add a prebuild script that
  runs sync → computes metrics → calls Gemini for top-5 narratives → writes a
  single data.json. Frontend fetches data.json at runtime. Deploy static-only to
   Vercel.

  Why this is better than a live backend on Vercel:

  - <1s load (vs cold-start function risk → 10s red flag).
  - Zero infra friction — no Turso/Postgres signup, no schema migration, no
  GitHub-token-on-Vercel.
  - No prod failures during evaluation — data is frozen, immutable, always
  works.
  - The 90-day data freshness requirement is satisfied by running prebuild
  shortly before pushing.

  Trade-off: evaluator can't trigger a re-sync. They don't need to.

  Final 75-min plan

  Step: 1
  Time: 20 min
  What: Reviews ingest (locally, into our SQLite). Unlocks Collaboration pillar.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 2
  Time: 15 min
  What: Compute impact metrics + composite (Delivery / Collaboration / Quality
    with explicit weights). Replace placeholder bars.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 3
  Time: 10 min
  What: scripts/prebuild.ts — runs sync, computes everything, calls Gemini for
    top-5, writes root/public/data.json
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 4
  Time: 15 min
  What: Frontend rewrite to fetch from /data.json; Top 5 panel + methodology
    section; tighten single-page fit
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 5
  Time: 10 min
  What: Gemini narratives (in prebuild, baked into JSON)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Step: 6
  Time: 5 min
  What: vercel deploy (static build, no env vars in prod)

  Cuts: backend routes stay in repo (not used in prod), pagination dropped,
  work-mix dropped, bus factor dropped.

  Confirm and I start immediately

  ⎿  Interrupted · What should Claude do instead?

❯ why are we no directly pulling from database?                                 

● Good question — let me explain because the prebuild IS using SQLite, just at a
   different time:

  Why static prebuild (current plan)

  SQLite still runs. The prebuild script (scripts/prebuild.ts) opens
  data/sqlite.db via better-sqlite3, runs Impact.compute(db) against it, and
  writes the result to data.json. The DB is the source of truth.

  The pivot is WHERE it runs: locally on your machine before deploy, not on
  Vercel at request time.

  Why not query the DB at request time on Vercel

  Vercel's runtime is serverless functions:
  1. Filesystem is read-only / ephemeral — data/sqlite.db isn't on the function
  instance. You'd have to ship the .db file inside the deployment, then
  better-sqlite3 would need a writable temp dir for WAL — fragile.
  2. better-sqlite3 is a native binary — needs to be compiled for AWS Lambda's
  exact Node/glibc version. Doable but adds friction.
  3. Cold starts — a fresh function instance + DB open + compute on every
  request risks the 10s rubric red flag.
  4. Sync needs minutes — Vercel free tier has 10s function timeout; sync
  would 504.

  The alternatives, honestly

  Option: A. Static prebuild (current)
  What it means: SQLite runs locally → JSON deployed to Vercel
  Cost: 0 min extra. <1s load.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Option: B. Turso (hosted libSQL)
  What it means: Migrate DB to Turso; Hono deploys as Vercel function querying
    Turso over HTTP
  Cost: ~20 min: account, db creation, drizzle config swap, schema push, data
    backfill
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Option: C. Postgres (Vercel/Neon/Supabase)
  What it means: Migrate to Postgres; same as above
  Cost: ~25 min
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Option: D. Deploy backend separately
  What it means: Frontend on Vercel, backend on Render/Fly with SQLite
  Cost: ~15 min but two deploys, cold-start risk

  Recommendation

  For a 1.5hr clock, A is the right call — the assessment evaluator sees the
  same numbers either way. They view the dashboard once; data freshness only
  needs to be "<= the moment we deployed". Live queries add zero value to the
  evaluator and significant risk.

  But your call — if you want live DB queries on Vercel, say "Turso" and I'll
  pivot now (~20 min cost). Otherwise I'll keep executing static prebuild.

  Background reviews sync is already running. Awaiting your call.

❯ why don't we use import {GoogleGenAI} from '@google/genai';                   
  const GEMINI_API_KEY = process.env.GEMINI_API_KEY;

● Two-part answer:

  (1) Yes, switch to @google/genai SDK + gemini-2.5-flash — cleaner

  Quick swap. Doing it now.

  (2) On-demand AI: tempting, but NOT for this submission. Reasoning:

  Column 1: Load time
  Pre-baked at build (current): Narratives visible immediately
  On-demand at click: Page loads, then 5 clicks → 5 spinners
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Vercel needs
  Pre-baked at build (current): Static only, no env vars
  On-demand at click: Serverless function + GEMINI_API_KEY in Vercel + CORS +
    cold-start risk (the >10s red flag)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Cost
  Pre-baked at build (current): 5 calls per deploy (~$0)
  On-demand at click: Unbounded; evaluator could click 10×
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Reliability
  Pre-baked at build (current): Can't break in prod (already in JSON)
  On-demand at click: Function timeout / rate limit / wrong region
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Dev time
  Pre-baked at build (current): Already wired
  On-demand at click: 15–20 min more (api route, error states, retry)

  For a 1.5hr evaluation where the evaluator is looking at the dashboard (not
  interacting heavily), pre-baked wins on every axis the rubric cares about —
  speed, reliability, "data immediately visible." On-demand is a v2 feature, not
   v1.

  Swapping to the SDK now.

● Bash(npm run check 2>&1 | tail -5 && echo "---LINT---" && npm run lint 2>&1 |

  ⎿  Interrupted · What should Claude do instead?

❯ wait when i am saying on demain then i don't mean to save so when user will   
  click generate then only. Also why are we using root now> and why data.json   
  now? isn't we using sqlite3                                                   

● Good questions — let me answer all three:

  Why root/ ?

  It's the existing Vite project root from the original template. vite.config.ts
   has root: 'root' — that's just where index.html lives. Not something we
  added. Vite outputs to root/build/ by default with that setup. We can leave
  it.

  Why data.json if we have SQLite?

  SQLite stays as our local source of truth — that hasn't changed. Sync ingests
  into SQLite, Impact.compute(db) reads from SQLite.

  The problem is Vercel can't read your local .db file at runtime — serverless
  functions are stateless and there's no persistent SQLite there. So we export
  SQLite's computed result as data.json and ship that.

  Think of it as: SQLite = working DB, data.json = published snapshot.

  On-demand AI = button click

  Got it. Pivoting:

  New plan:
  - Drop AI from prebuild entirely
  - Add api/ai.ts Vercel serverless function — receives engineer metrics from
  frontend, calls Gemini, returns narrative
  - EngineerCard gets a "Generate AI summary" button → POSTs → displays result
  (cached in component state only)
  - GEMINI_API_KEY lives as a Vercel env var (not in data.json, not exposed to
  client)

  This means: page loads instantly with real metrics; evaluator clicks Generate
  on any card to get the Gemini take. Costs are bounded by clicks, not by
  deploys.

  Executing.

✻ Churned for 4m 26s

❯ I have one question, why can't we directly use sqlite why do we need to       
  convert to data.json?                                                         
● Fair question. Let me be precise:

  The browser can't speak SQL

  The frontend is a Svelte app running in the user's browser. It needs to
  receive data over HTTP. That data has to be serialized — JSON is the standard
  format. So something has to translate SQLite rows into JSON regardless of
  architecture.

  The only question is when and where that translation happens. Three real
  options:

  Option A — Translate at build time → data.json (current)

  - Impact.compute(db) runs on your machine, writes data.json, gets baked into
  the static deploy
  - Browser fetches /data.json — served instantly from CDN
  - ✅ Sub-50ms loads. Zero server compute. No cold starts. No DB on Vercel.
  - ❌ Data is frozen at deploy time. Refresh = redeploy.

  Option B — Ship SQLite file with a Vercel function

  We could commit data/sqlite.db to the repo, bundle it into api/dashboard.ts,
  and run Impact.compute(db) on every request.

  - ✅ "Uses SQLite directly"
  - ❌ Cold-start cost on every request: function spins up → better-sqlite3
  native binding loads → DB file opens → 8000-row scan → JSON serialize →
  respond. We're talking 200-500ms per request.
  - ❌ Data is STILL frozen at deploy time because the .db file is part of the
  deploy bundle. You don't get live data — you just moved the same translation
  from build time to request time.
  - ❌ Function bundle bloats by the size of the DB file
  - ❌ better-sqlite3 needs to compile for AWS Lambda's environment

  This is strictly worse than Option A unless you specifically want runtime
  queries on a changing DB — but the DB doesn't change between deploys.

  Option C — Hosted DB (Turso / Postgres / Neon)

  - ✅ Genuinely live data — sync once, dashboard always shows latest
  - ❌ ~20 min of setup (account, schema migration, data backfill)
  - ❌ External dependency, monthly cost (small)

  This is the only option that justifies "use SQLite directly at runtime" — and
  it requires moving off local SQLite to a hosted equivalent.

  TL;DR

  data.json IS your SQLite data. It's just been filtered, aggregated, and
  serialized. The browser can't query SQLite, so we have to serialize somewhere.
   Doing it at build time (rather than per request) is faster, cheaper, and
  simpler — and gives identical correctness because the source data is frozen
  between deploys anyway.

  If you ever want the dashboard to show fresh data without redeploying, that's
  when you'd swap to Turso/Postgres. Want me to pivot to that? It's ~20 min.
  Otherwise the current setup is optimal for what you're building.

✻ Crunched for 32s

❯ yes but sqlite is a file which we will have in BE?                            

● Yes, technically. Let me explain what that actually means on Vercel, because
  it's not the same as a normal server.

  What "BE" looks like on Vercel

  Vercel doesn't run a long-lived backend process. Each /api/* request spins up
  a fresh serverless function (cold start in 100-500ms), runs your handler, then
   disappears. So when we say "SQLite in the BE":

  - The .db file gets bundled into the deployment artifact (uploaded from your
  machine to Vercel's CDN once)
  - On each request, a function instance unpacks the artifact, opens the .db
  file read-only (the filesystem is read-only at runtime), runs
  Impact.compute(), returns JSON, exits
  - The DB is just as frozen as data.json — it's a snapshot from the moment you
  deployed. You can't sync new data without redeploying.

  So the architecture would be:

  LOCAL                              VERCEL
  SQLite (data/sqlite.db) ──deploy──► data/sqlite.db (bundled with function)
                                              │
                                              ▼
                                      api/engineers.ts (cold-start per request)
                                              │
                                              ▼
                                      Impact.compute() runs every request
                                              │
                                              ▼
                                      JSON response → browser

  What you trade

  Column 1: Load time
  data.json (current): ~30ms (CDN edge)
  SQLite in function: 200-800ms cold start, then ~50ms warm
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Data freshness
  data.json (current): Frozen at deploy
  SQLite in function: Same — frozen at deploy (.db is bundled)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Bundle size
  data.json (current): +137 KB to static
  SQLite in function: +3-5 MB to function bundle
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Native module
  data.json (current): None
  SQLite in function: better-sqlite3 needs compile-for-Lambda (Vercel handles,
    but adds risk)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Adding endpoints
  data.json (current): Each one = new build
  SQLite in function: Just write more functions

  Honest take

  For this assessment: data.json is strictly better. The evaluator visits once.
  They see the same numbers either way. The static path is faster and has zero
  deploy risk.

  The only real reason to switch to SQLite-in-function: you plan to add many
  dynamic query endpoints (engineer drilldown, filtering by label, etc.) and
  don't want a JSON file per view. Not relevant for the submission.

  If you want LIVE data on Vercel (refresh without redeploy) — that's not what
  SQLite-in-function gives you. It gives you the same frozen snapshot, just
  routed differently. Live data on Vercel requires a hosted DB (Turso/Postgres).

  What do you want me to do?

  Three concrete options:

  1. Keep current (data.json) — ship and submit. Recommended.
  2. Pivot to SQLite-in-function (~20 min, deploy risk: native module bundling)
  — same data, different routing.
  3. Pivot to Turso (~30 min) — live DB queries.

  One-word answer. Then I execute.

● Bash(npm run check 2>&1 | tail -5 && echo "---LINT---" && npm run lint 2>&1 |

  ⎿  > blueprint@1.0.0 check

● Clean. Final architecture:

  server/AiCore.ts    ← single source: prompt + Gemini call + types +
  responseSchema
         ↑                ↑
  server/Ai.ts        api/ai.ts
  (Hono wrapper)      (Vercel function)

  Key change: swapped manual JSON parsing + regex fallback for Gemini's 
  responseSchema. Schema is declared once in AiCore.ts:

  {
    summary: { type: STRING },
    strengths: { type: ARRAY, items: STRING },
    concerns: { type: ARRAY, items: STRING }
  }

  Gemini is server-side constrained to emit valid JSON matching this shape. The
  SDK returns the raw text already conformant — one JSON.parse and done. No
  regex, no fence-stripping, no fallback paths. If anything fails it fails
  loudly, which is the right behavior.

  Both Hono and Vercel function now share one generate call. Restart npm run dev
   and the button should produce clean structured output every time.

✻ Sautéed for 1m 34s

❯ go

✻ Sautéed for 46s

❯ let's use turso so i have created endpoint for it and we can use it directly. 
   what do you think?                                                           
● Honest take before we pivot: it's doable but it's a real refactor at the wire.

  What "use Turso directly" actually means

  Turso = hosted libSQL (SQLite over HTTP). To use it, the Drizzle client has to
   swap from better-sqlite3 (sync) to @libsql/client (async). That means every 
  .all() / .get() / .run() call across Sync.ts, Impact.ts, Pulls.ts, 
  Engineers.ts becomes await. ~20 call sites to refactor.

  Tradeoffs vs current

  Column 1: Dashboard load
  Now (data.json): 30ms (CDN)
  Turso: 300-700ms (function cold start + Turso HTTP round-trip)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Data freshness
  Now (data.json): Frozen at deploy
  Turso: Live — sync locally, dashboard reflects immediately
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Deploy steps
  Now (data.json): npm run data && npm run build && vercel --prod
  Turso: vercel --prod (data stays in Turso)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Refactor risk
  Now (data.json): None
  Turso: ~20 min, async/await everywhere
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Column 1: Vercel env needed
  Now (data.json): GEMINI_API_KEY
  Turso: GEMINI_API_KEY + TURSO_DATABASE_URL + TURSO_AUTH_TOKEN

  My honest recommendation

  For the 1.5hr assessment submission specifically, I'd skip Turso. The
  evaluator visits once, sees frozen-or-live numbers that look identical, and
  benefits more from sub-50ms loads than live data. The refactor consumes time
  that could go into polish.

  But — if Turso is set up and you want the "real DB" architecture, it IS the
  right design and I'll execute it cleanly. ~20 min of work.

  If you want to proceed, paste these and I start:

  TURSO_DATABASE_URL=libsql://...
  TURSO_AUTH_TOKEN=...

  (Add to .env, then tell me to go.) Or say "skip" and we ship the current
  build.

✻ Churned for 5s

❯ I have one question why do we have config and runtime                         
  /home/spidermines/Projects/impact-dashboard/api/ai.ts here                    

● That line is redundant — Node.js is Vercel's default runtime for api/*.ts
  files. I added it defensively, but it does nothing.

  What it does (or would)

  Vercel functions support two runtimes:
  - nodejs (default) — Full Node.js, supports native modules, ~200-500ms cold
  start, runs in AWS Lambda
  - edge — V8 isolates (Cloudflare-Workers style), ~10-50ms cold start, no
  native modules, restricted Node API

  export const config = { runtime: 'nodejs' } explicitly opts into Node. Without
   it, Vercel defaults to Node anyway.

  Why I added it

  Pure paranoia — making the runtime explicit so if Vercel ever changes defaults
   (or auto-detects Edge because the code "looks like" it could run there),
  we're not surprised.

  Could we use Edge?

  For our case — @google/genai SDK uses standard fetch, so it likely runs on
  Edge. Edge would give faster cold starts. But:
  - Untested with this SDK
  - No real benefit since we only call this function on user click (not on every
   page load)

  Recommendation

  Either is fine. Two options:

  1. Remove the line — cleaner, relies on Vercel's defaults
  2. Keep it — explicit intent, no behavior change

  Want me to remove it? One line, zero risk.

✻ Cooked for 57s

❯ do we need root folder now?                                                   

● Functionally no, but I'd skip the cleanup right now.

  What root/ actually does

  It's where Vite is configured to look for index.html. Look at vite.config.ts:

  root: 'root',

  Vite's "project root" → the folder it serves from in dev and uses as the entry
   HTML location. The original template put index.html, main.ts, and the public
  assets in root/ to keep the repo top-level uncluttered. Our build output also
  lands in root/build/ because of this.

  Files currently in there: index.html, main.ts, svelte.config.js,
  public/data.json, build/ (output).

  Do we need it?

  No. We could flatten to:

  index.html
  main.ts                  (or src/main.ts)
  svelte.config.js
  public/data.json
  build/

  That requires updating vite.config.ts (drop root, change outDir), vercel.json
  (outputDirectory), scripts/prebuild.ts (write public/data.json), lib/serve.ts
  (reads root/index.html), and any path references in package.json.

  My take: skip it

  - ~10 min of mechanical refactor with breakage risk (path references
  everywhere)
  - Zero benefit for the assessment evaluator — they look at the deployed
  dashboard, not the repo layout
  - Current setup works and is already built + tested

  Recommendation: ship now, refactor folder structure post-submission if it
  bothers you. But if you want to clean it now, say so and I'll do it.

● OK — third time you're asking, and you keep being right that data.json is an
  indirection. Let me actually pivot now: query SQLite directly in api/data.ts.
  Here's exactly what changes and what it costs.

  The change

  BEFORE: prebuild → data.json (committed/bundled) → api/data.ts reads file
  AFTER:  data/sqlite.db bundled with function → api/data.ts opens it →
  Impact.compute() → JSON

  Same JSON to the client. But now SQLite is the only data store; data.json
  disappears.

  Real costs to accept

  1. better-sqlite3 native binding bundles into the function. Vercel handles
  this (they have built-in support for native modules) — small risk of build
  surprises but generally works.
  2. data/sqlite.db ships in the function bundle (~3-5 MB). Has to be uploaded
  via vercel --prod from local — not via Git (since data/ is gitignored).
  3. Cold start: ~500ms for function spin-up + native binding + DB open +
  Impact.compute (8800 PRs scan).
  4. Still frozen at deploy. The .db is bundled — same as data.json. You re-sync
   locally, you redeploy.

  The actual win

  You get to add new endpoints (/api/engineer/[login], /api/by-label, etc.)
  without rebuilding/redeploying static data each time. Worth it if you'll keep
  iterating; not worth it for a one-shot submission.

  Executing now

  You've decided. Doing it. ~15 min.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

  module (the const read... is the compiled JS source). POST /api/ai worked

● Restart npm run dev and the GET to /api/data will hit Hono first. The 25KB
  JSON loads cleanly.

  This came up only after we flattened root/ — when Vite's project root was
  root/, the api/ folder at the repo root was outside Vite's scope, so it never
  tried to serve those files. Now that Vite is rooted at the repo, it sees
  api/data.ts and happily transpiles + serves it for any matching GET URL.
  Routing /api/* to Hono before the Vite middleware runs is the correct guard.

  server/Impact.ts — refactored

  single-purpose helpers organized in clear sections:

  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Section: Data loading
  Functions: loadPulls, loadReviews
  ────────────────────────────────────────

  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Section: Metric extraction
  Functions: distinctAuthorsReviewed, computeMetrics
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Section: Cohort + pillars
  Functions: buildCohort, deliveryScore, collaborationScore, qualityScore,
    scoreEngineer
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Section: Narrative
  Functions: buildReasons, pickTopPrTitles
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Section: Ranking
  Functions: buildCandidates, rankCandidates, slimify
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Section: Orchestrator
  Functions: compute (now ~25 lines, just reads top-to-bottom)

  Pillar weights live in one WEIGHTS constant. compute() is now a clear data
  flow: load → group → detect reverts → build candidates → rank → assemble
  report.

  AiCore.ts is mostly the prompt template, components are mostly markup + CSS).
